Statutory Authorities under the Attorney-General
(Question No. 2850)
Mr Les Johnson asked the Minister representing the Attorney-General, upon notice, on 26 August 1981:
(I) Further to the Review of Commonwealth Functions which called the Ministers to scrutinise all authorities within their portfolios (Hansard, 30 April 1981. page 1850) which statutory authorities within the Minister's portfolio are to be (a) terminated, (b) continued and (c) reviewed in depth.
(2) If the scrutiny referred to in part (I) has not been completed, when will it be finalised and the results reported to Parliament.
Mr Viner-The Attorney-General has provided the following answers to the honourable member's questions:
(I) and (2) I refer the honourable member to the answer provided to question No. 2839 -on 22 September 1981 by the then Acting Prime Minister (Hansard page 1647). Decisions to terminate the Commonwealth Legal Aid Commission and the Legislative Drafting Institute were made directly as aresull of the Review of Comonwealth Functions and announced by the Prime Minister on 30 April 1981.
Delivery of National Health Scheme Prescriptions
(Question No. 2965)
Dr Everingham asked the Minister for Health, upon notice, on 8 September 1981 :
(I) Will he take steps to authorise delivery of National Heallh Scheme dispensed items from prescriptions relayed by telephone to a pharmacist from an authorised subscriber through a registered nurse subject to checking the item against the prescription in person or by telephone at the point of delivery in the presence of a pharmacist, trained nurse or authorised prescriber.
(2) Will he authorise NHS prescription collection and dispensed item delivery charges to be met by patients or, in default of provision of written prescriptions, by prescribers.
Mr MacKellar-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(I) and (2) In relation to the communication of prescriptions to approved chemists, a pharmaceutical benefit may only be supplied by an approved chemist after the surrender of the prescription, except in the case of urgency.

In such cases, where a medical practitioner or participating dental practitioner communicates a prescription by telephone or other means to a chemist, the communicated prescription must be reduced to writing and despatched within twenty four hours to the approved chemist who supplied the benefit. However, this provision does not apply to prescriptions for supply by chemists where the law of the State or Territory requires the prescription to be in writing.
In regard to the imposition of charges, the approved chemist supplying the benefit is entitled under the National Health (Pharmaceutical Benefits) Regulations, to charge the patient an amount equal to the co~t of delivery when the benefit is supplied at a place other than the premises in respect of which the chemist is approved. This is a matter between the chemist and the patient.
It is not envisaged that persons other than medical practitioners or participating dental practitioners will be authorised to communicate prescriptions to approved chemists. Also it is not proposed to authorise the approved chemist to impose charges to collect prescriptions.
Immigration
(Question No. 2967)
Mr Campbell asked the Minister for Immigration and Ethnic Affairs, upon notice, on 8 September 1981:
What percentage of applicants for migration to Australia from (a) Indo-China, (b) Lebanon and (c) Poland, are being granted Australian residence.
Mr Macphee-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(a) There is currently little migration from Vietnam, Laos and Kampuchea to Australia. Discussions with the Vietnamese authorities are proceeding with a view to agreement on procedures for an Orderly Departure Program under which applicants in Vietnam can be considered and processed in accordance with Australia's non-discriminatory migration policy and procedures.
With a few exceptions, Indo-Chinese people settling in Australia have done so as refugees. Most applicants are processed by refugee task forces or Australian migration officers in Thailand, Malaysia and other countries in South East Asia.
(b) and (c) The following table gives details of migration applications determined at Australian Embassies in Syria (where applications from residents of Lebanon are processed) and Poland over the last two years:

The differences in the rates of approvals reflects differences
in definitions of applications and in the migration arrange-
ments operating in the two countries. The lower percentage of Lebanese applicants approved in 1980-81 reflects a substantial increase in the number of ineligible applications Following
the introduction of the concessional independent Family nominations (lFN) in mid-1980. A large number of persons, previously rejected, reapplied under the new provisions. Most ap-
plicants were unable to obtain sufficient points under NUMAS to obtain approval even with the concessions under IFN. Migrationdirectly From Poland is restricted to persons
sponsored by relatives or Friends in Australia. In general, sponsorships are accepted only where there is a good prospect
of approval of those sponsored so that most sponsored applicants in Poland meet migrant entry requirements. This restriction is imposed by the Polish Authorities.

National Nursing Manpower Task Force
(Question No. 3053)
Mr Les McMahon asked the Minister for Health, upon notice, on 9 September 1981:
(I) Further to his answer to question No. 883 (Hansard, 28 April 1981, page 1680) has the National Nursing Manpower Taskforce decided when a Further update of the inFormation is required.

(2) If the National Nursing Manpower TaskForce has updated the information how many (a) nurses and (b) nursing sisters are currently (i) registered and (ii) employed in Australia.
Mr MacKellar-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(I) and (2) The October 1981 Australian Health Ministers' ConFerence supported the recommendation of the National Nursing Manpower Task Force to seek assistance From the April 1982 Australasian Nurse Registering Authorities ConFerence in collecting uniform data For updating national nursing statistics and to monitor Future nursing manpower needs.
Pregnancy Drug 'Benedictin'
(Question No. 3094)
Mr Holding asked the Minister for Health, upon notice, on 15 September 1981:
(1) Has his attention been drawn to allegations by Dr William McBride in the National Times of 6 September 1981 that the pregnancy drug Benedictin (also sold under the trade names of Debendox, Lenatan and Merbental) distributed by Richardson-Mervill Inc., has similar effects on unborn children as Thalidomide.
(2) Are any of these drugs currently being distributed in Australia; if so, what action has been taken to establish their saFety.
Mr MacKellar-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(I) Yes-I have seen the article in the National Times of 6 September 1981.
(2) Debendox is currently being distributed in Australia. The question of the safe use of Debendox was considered by the Australian Drug Evaluation Committee at the time when this matter was first raised. The Committee concluded that the evidence before it was such that the Frequency of birth deFects in the children of mothers who have taken Debendox during pregnancy had not been demonstrated to exceed that iii mothers who did not take Debendox. A number of children identified by Dr McBride as possibly having birth deFects associated with the use of Debendox are currently being reviewed on behalF of my Department. In addition my Department is currently evaluating furth~r data including those made available by Dr McBride. A recent scientific article in the British Medical Journal of I I July 1981 concerning a study of Debendox in early pregnancy concludes: These results support the hypothesis that Debendox is not teratogenic. '
Health: Commonwealth Funding
(Question No. 3112)
Mr Jacobi asked the Minister for Health, upon notice, on 16 September 1981:
(I) Is it a fact that cuts in Commonwealth Funding For health have reduced the staff available For the testing and examination of the quality of imported medical products including dressings, drugs and medical devices.
(2) Is it also a fact that as a result of the lack of adequate surveillance and security there is a massive influx of imported sub-standard and dangerous therapeutic goods.
(3) Will he undertake an immediate and full investigation into this whole area to ensure that the Australian public is protected From the disastrous effects arising From inFerior imported therapeutic products.

Answers to Questions

28 October 1981 REPRESENTATIVES 2659

Mr MacKellar-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(I) Some reduction in staffing has occurred through normal wastage. Recruitment action to replace such staff is being taken within my Department's staff ceiling allocation.
(2) No. The National Biological Standards Laboratory undertakes sampling and testing of therapeutic goods, including imported products, on a random basis, as well as promptly investigating complaints through specific testing programs. It would not be feasible to routinely sample and test the thousands of consignments of therapeutic goods which are imported into Australia annually.
(3) The present programs are practical and effective ways of detecting inferior imported therapeutic products and allowing appropriate actions to be taken in the public interest.
Meat Exports to the Middle East
Mr Nixon-On 26 August 1981 (Hansard, page 781) Mr Ian Robinson asked me the following question without notice:
Does the Minister for Primary Industry have any information as to whether there is a racket involved in Australian meat exports to the Middle East, as has been claimed in recent Press reports? Is there a possible link between the alleged fraudulent trading to the Middle East and that to the United States of America?
In my answer to the honourable member's question I indicated that I would investigate claims that kangaroo meat has been found in mutton cartons in Saudi Arabia (Hansard page 781). I now provide the following additional information:
The Executive Officer of the Australian Federation of Islamic Councils has advised that no kangaroo meat has been sent to Saudi Arabia as has been claimed. He further advised that the Saudi Arabian Charge d'Affaires in Singapore had categorically denied making any such statements.
A recently returned Australian Trade Commissioner to Riyad, Saudi Arabia, reported that the authorities in that country were satisfied with the meat inspection aspects of Australian meat.
A recent visit by two senior officers of the Australian Government has confirmed that the Saudi Arabian authorities are satisfied with measures taken to ensure the integrity of Australian export meat.
Report of the National Energy Advisory Committee
Mr Anthony-On 24 September 1981 (Hansard, page 1738) Mr Beazley asked me, as the Minister representing the Minister for National Development and Energy, the following question without notice:
I refer the Minister representing the Minister for National Development and Energy to a recently released report~ No. 14-of the National Energy Advisory Committee on Australia's energy resources.
Does this' report express serious concern that inadequate physical data and economic assessments exist on Australia's energy resources?
Does the report also express concern that information collected by companies and States is frequently not available on a nationally co-ordinated and consistent basis?

Were similar criticisms made by the National Energy Advisory Committee over three years ago in its initial report on energy resources?
In view of these criticisms what action does the Government intend to take to establish a national information base for the assessment of Australia's energy resources?
Given the concerns of the National Energy Advisory Committee, can the Minister explain why the Government has run down staffing of the Bureau of Mineral Resources?
The Minister for National Development and Energy has provided the following answer to the honourable member's question:
The National Energy Advisory Committee recorded in its Report No. 14 that there have been a number of constructive developments in the area of resource assessments, principally in the assessment of oil shale, since the publication of their earlier Report No. 2~'Australia's Energy Resources: An Assessment' .
In their report the Committee said that there were some areas where information was inadequate for effective analysis of Australia's renewable and non-renewable energy resources. However, the Committee also pointed out that obtaining basic data about resources was a costly process and, to warrant incurring costs for this purpose, there should be some reasonable expectation of comparable gain. For this reason the amount of information that it is sensible to obtain wbuld always fall short of that which would give a complete technical and economic enumeration of the resource situation.
The Committee did point out that for some energy resources (eg petroleum) information is not always available on a nationally co-ordinated and consistent basis. The Government is attempting to remedy this through co-opera-tion with the States.
Within the Department of National Development and Energy, the Bureau of Mineral Resources has responsibility for undertaking assessments of the nation's mineral resources.
Government authorities in each State are responsible for the assessment of coal in their State, with the Bureau of Mineral Resources being responsible for the assessment of Australia's coal resources on a national scale. The Australian Atomic Energy Commission carries out independent assessrnents of recoverable reserves of uranium. Assessments of renewable energy resources are being assisted through the NERDD program.
Restructuring the Bureau of Mineral Resources to enhance its role. as a centre of geoscience research is nearing completion. This research is a prerequisite for effective exploration and resource assessment. Research will be undertaken by four new divisions; a fifth division will be responsible for undertaking assessments of the nation's mineral resources with particular attention being paid to energy resources. Recruitment is actively underway to support these activities.
Canberra Women's Refuge
(Question No. 1722)
Mr Bungey asked the Minister for Health, upon notice, on 9 April 1981 :
(I) How was the 1979-80 grant of $57,800 to the Canberra Women's Refuge by the Capital Territory Health Commission determined.
(2) What functions does the centre undertake, and how is it financed.
Mr MacKellar-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:

2660 REPRESENTATIVES 28 October 1981

Answers to Questions

(I) The 1979-80 Community Health Grant of $57,800 was determined by the Capital Territory Health Commission, having regard to the estimates of expenditure for the year submitted by the Canberra Women's Refuge to the Commission.
(2) The Refuge provides temporary accommodation and domestic support for women and children in crisis situations. The support may extend to cover counselling and subsequent referr\ll to other appropriate agencies. These activities are funded by the Commission.
Outside school hours care ($10,000 p.a.) and vacation care ($3884 for December 1980 to September 1981) for the children of women accommodated at the refuge are funded through the Children's Services Program, whiCh is administered by the Department of Social Security. A grant for supplementary needs (e.g. transporting children to day care centres) is also provided under that Program.
The refuge operates a follow-up support and counselling service for former residents ($8,000 p.a.). This service is funded under the Family Support Services Scheme which is a component of the Children's Services Program and which is administered jointly with State and Territory Governments.
In addition, a welfare grant of $3,000 was provided by the Department of the Capital Territory in 1979-80 for capital equipment.
